## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations / dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration of an oscillator with state (x, v) evolving in time t, which is the standard second-order ODE form x' = v, v' = f(x, v, t). Nonlinear harmonic oscillator models typically combine a restoring force (often nonlinear in x), damping (often nonlinear in v or x), and possibly external/parametric time-dependent forcing.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (undamped, unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring acceleration, sign absorbed into c0)
- Linear viscous damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear spring + linear damping)
- Constant-force bias / equilibrium shift: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 (gravity/offset force or shifted equilibrium)
- Nonlinear (quadratic) damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * Abs(v) (drag-like dissipation at higher speeds)
- Coulomb/friction-like damping (smooth approximation): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * tanh(c2 * v) (velocity sign-dependent friction)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity + damping)
- Higher-order polynomial stiffness: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 + c3 * v (strongly nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear stiffness with rational softening: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x / (c2 + x**2) + c3 * v (stiffness decreases with amplitude)
- Pendulum equation (angle as x): dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (nonlinear periodic restoring torque + damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v + c2 * x (self-excited oscillation via amplitude-dependent damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-dependent damping): dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v + c2 * x (negative damping at small |v|, positive at large |v|)
- Externally driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic forcing)
- Duffing with periodic drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (chaos-capable driven nonlinear oscillator)
- Parametric excitation (time-varying stiffness): dv_dt = (c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x + c3 * v (Mathieu-type parametric resonance)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force from a potential → dv_dt depends primarily on x and is odd in x for symmetric potentials (e.g., x, x**3, sin(c*x))
- Hardening/softening behavior with amplitude → inclusion of x**3 (hardening if same sign as linear term; softening if opposite sign)
- Limit cycles/self-oscillation → damping term that changes sign with amplitude, e.g., (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v
- Energy dissipation increasing with speed → terms like v*Abs(v) or higher odd powers of v added with damping sign
- Friction dominated regime → acceleration includes a sign(v)-like contribution, often modeled smoothly with tanh(c*v)
- External periodic forcing → additive sin/cos(c*t) term produces sustained oscillations and resonance peaks
- Parametric resonance → time-periodic modulation multiplying x (or stiffness), i.e., (c0 + c1*cos(c2*t))*x
- Symmetry breaking / biased equilibrium → constant term added to dv_dt shifts the equilibrium position away from x=0
- Nonlinear stiffness saturation/softening → rational dependence on x (e.g., x/(c + x**2)) limits effective restoring force at large |x|

GT (fixed) is the concrete function
\[
0.415528810853583\sin(t)\;-\;0.0493727442837992\,v^3\;-\;0.291667748408705\,|v|^{1/3}\;-\;1.02930087898757\,x(0.0222734330694684\,t+1)\;-\;1.02930087898757\,x.
\]
So GT contains these *essential* structures simultaneously:

- a pure \(\sin(t)\) term (no \(x\) inside),
- a \(v^3\) term,
- a \(|v|^{1/3}\) term (fractional power of absolute value),
- an \(x t\) cross-term: \(-K\,x\,t\),
- an \(x\) term (actually two linear-in-\(x\) contributions, equivalent to \(-K(0.02227\,t+2)x\)).

Any candidate must be able to represent all of these exactly (by choosing its free constants). In particular, **none** of the candidates include a \(|v|^{1/3}\) (or any fractional power of \(|v|\)) term, so that alone will block equivalence unless GT’s coefficient were 0 (it is not).

Trig phase-shift note: several candidates can match the GT’s \(0.4155\sin(t)\) using a cos term with phase shift, or a sin(c4*t+c5) term by setting c4=1 and c5=0. That part is not the issue. The blockers are the **simultaneous presence** in GT of (i) \(|v|^{1/3}\) and (ii) an \(x t\) linear cross-term; no candidate has either structure (and none has the fractional-power absolute value at all).

GT Equivalence Verification (PO12)
============================================================
GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*Abs(v)**c1 - omega0**c2*(gamma*t + c3)*x - omega0**c4*x
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0493727*v³ - 1.02930*(0.02227*t + 1)*x - 1.02930*x + 0.41553*sin(t) - 0.29167*|v|^(1/3)`

Let me simplify the GT:
- The x terms: `-1.02930*(0.02227*t + 1)*x - 1.02930*x = -1.02930*0.02227*t*x - 1.02930*x - 1.02930*x = -0.02293*t*x - 2.05860*x`
- So GT = `-0.04937*v³ - 0.02293*t*x - 2.05860*x + 0.41553*sin(t) - 0.29167*|v|^(1/3)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v³` 
2. `t*x` (product of t and x)
3. `x` (linear in x)
4. `sin(t)` 
5. `|v|^(1/3)` (cube root of absolute value of v)

This is a very specific combination. Let me check each candidate for the presence of all required basis functions.

Key requirements:
- Must have `v³` term
- Must have `t*x` term
- Must have `x` term
- Must have `sin(t)` term
- Must have `|v|^(1/3)` term

The `|v|^(1/3)` term is particularly distinctive - it's a fractional power of absolute value. Very few candidates will have this.

Let me scan through candidates looking for `|v|^(1/3)`:

None of the candidates contain `|v|^(1/3)` or any equivalent fractional power of v. The candidates contain terms like:
- `v*|v|` = `|v|²·sign(v)` (not equivalent)
- `v³`
- `|v|²`
- `sin(|v|+c)`
- `v/(|v|+c)`
- `Max(0,v)`, `Max(0,-v)`

The `|v|^(1/3)` function is linearly independent from all of these. No combination of the basis functions present in any candidate can produce `|v|^(1/3)` for all values of v.

Let me verify this carefully for each candidate - none can produce the `|v|^(1/3)` term, which means none can match the GT exactly.

Let me double-check candidates that have `sin(|v|+c)` terms (Candidates 32, 50) - `sin(c7*|v|+c8)` is not equivalent to `|v|^(1/3)`.

Candidates with `v/(|v|+c)` (Candidates 22, 48) - this approaches ±1 for large |v|, not `|v|^(1/3)`.

Candidates with `Max(0,v)` and `Max(0,-v)` (35-41) - `c2*Max(0,-v) + c8*Max(0,v)` can represent `a*v + b*|v|` but not `|v|^(1/3)`.

None of the candidates contain the required `|v|^(1/3)` basis function, which is linearly independent from all basis functions present in any candidate.
